If &vert;_a_&vert; is large, then _f_\(_ax_\) is concentrated around 0 and <br/> ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }{\widehat {f} }\left({\frac {\omega }{a} }\right)\,$ <br/> spreads out and flattens. <!--SR:!2026-01-20,55,310-->
> - \(105\) ${\widehat {f} }_{n}(x)\,$ ::@:: ${\widehat {f} }_{1}(x)\ {\stackrel { {\mathcal {F} }_{1} }{\longleftrightarrow } }\ f(-\xi )\, \quad ; \quad {\widehat {f} }_{2}(x)\ {\stackrel { {\mathcal {F} }_{2} }{\longleftrightarrow } }\ f(-\omega )\, \quad ; \quad {\widehat {f} }_{3}(x)\ {\stackrel { {\mathcal {F} }_{3} }{\longleftrightarrow } }\ 2\pi f(-\omega )\,$ <!--SR:!2026-01-22,57,310!2025-12-02,20,363-->
>   - \(105\) ${\widehat {f} }_{n}(x)\, \implies {\widehat {f} }_{1}(x)\ {\stackrel { {\mathcal {F} }_{1} }{\longleftrightarrow } }\ f(-\xi )\,$ :@: The same transform is applied twice, but _x_ replaces the frequency variable \(_ξ_ or _ω_\) after the first transform. <!--SR:!2026-01-27,61,327-->
>   - \(105\) ${\widehat {f} }_{n}(x)\, \implies {\widehat {f} }_{1}(x)\ {\stackrel { {\mathcal {F} }_{1} }{\longleftrightarrow } }\ f(-\xi )\,$ / mnemonic ::@:: Negate argument and multiply by a factor if _non-unitary_ \(e.g. $2\pi$ for the non-unitary angular momentum convention\). <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,361!2025-12-01,19,361-->
> - \(106\) ${\frac {d^{n}f(x)}{dx^{n} } }\,$ ::@:: $(i2\pi \xi )^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\xi )\, \quad ; \quad (i\omega )^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\omega )\, \quad ; \quad (i\omega )^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\omega )\,$ <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,355!2025-11-29,17,338-->
>   - \(106\) ${\frac {d^{n}f(x)}{dx^{n} } }\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } (i2\pi \xi )^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\xi )\,$ :@: n<sup>th</sup>-order derivative. As _f_ is a [Schwartz function](Schwartz%20space.md) <!--SR:!2026-01-12,46,304-->
>   - \(106\) ${\frac {d^{n}f(x)}{dx^{n} } }\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } (i2\pi \xi )^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\xi )\,$ / mnemonic ::@:: Negate the exponent argument and multiply it by _n_ times. <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,352!2025-11-29,17,353-->
> - \(106.5\) $\int _{-\infty }^{x}f(\tau )d\tau$ ::@:: ${\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\xi )}{i2\pi \xi } }+C\,\delta (\xi ) \quad ; \quad {\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\omega )}{i\omega } }+{\sqrt {2\pi } }C\delta (\omega ) \quad ; \quad {\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\omega )}{i\omega } }+2\pi C\delta (\omega )$ <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,353!2026-01-22,58,338-->
>   - \(106.5\) $\int _{-\infty }^{x}f(\tau )d\tau {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\xi )}{i2\pi \xi } }+C\,\delta (\xi )$ :@: Integration.<sup>[\[80\]](#^ref-80)</sup> Note: $\delta$ is the [Dirac delta function](Dirac%20delta%20function.md) and $C$ is the average \([DC](DC%20component.md)\) value of $f(x)$ such that $\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }(f(x)-C)\,dx=0$ <!--SR:!2026-02-04,69,337-->
>   - \(106.5\) $\int _{-\infty }^{x}f(\tau )d\tau {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\xi )}{i2\pi \xi } }+C\,\delta (\xi )$ / mnemonic ::@:: Negate the exponent argument and divide it. Then add the average value \(multiplied by a certain factor\) _C_ to the zero frequency. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,350!2025-11-29,17,348-->
> - \(107\) $x^{n}f(x)\,$ ::@:: $\left({\frac {i}{2\pi } }\right)^{n}{\frac {d^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\xi )}{d\xi ^{n} } }\, \quad ; \quad i^{n}{\frac {d^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\omega )}{d\omega ^{n} } } \quad ; \quad i^{n}{\frac {d^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\omega )}{d\omega ^{n} } }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361!2025-11-29,17,338-->
>   - \(107\) $x^{n}f(x)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } \left({\frac {i}{2\pi } }\right)^{n}{\frac {d^{n}{\widehat {f} }(\xi )}{d\xi ^{n} } }\,$ :@: This is the dual of 106 <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,349-->
> - \(108\) $(f*g)(x)\,$ ::@:: ${\widehat {f} }(\xi ){\widehat {g} }(\xi )\, \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {2\pi } }\ {\widehat {f} }(\omega ){\widehat {g} }(\omega )\, \quad ; \quad {\widehat {f} }(\omega ){\widehat {g} }(\omega )\,$ <!--SR:!2026-01-13,47,314!2025-12-02,20,363-->
>   - \(108\) $(f*g)(x)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\widehat {f} }(\xi ){\widehat {g} }(\xi )\,$ :@: The notation _f_ ∗ _g_ denotes the [convolution](convolution.md) of _f_ and _g_ — this rule is the [convolution theorem](convolution%20theorem.md) <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361-->
> - \(109\) $f(x)g(x)\,$ ::@:: $\left({\widehat {f} }*{\widehat {g} }\right)(\xi )\, \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }\left({\widehat {f} }*{\widehat {g} }\right)(\omega )\, \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{2\pi } }\left({\widehat {f} }*{\widehat {g} }\right)(\omega )\,$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-11-30,18,345-->
>   - \(109\) $f(x)g(x)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } \left({\widehat {f} }*{\widehat {g} }\right)(\xi )\,$ :@: This is the dual of 108 <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361-->
> - \(110\) For _f_\(_x_\) purely real ::@:: ${\widehat {f} }(-\xi )={\overline { {\widehat {f} }(\xi )} }\, \quad ; \quad {\widehat {f} }(-\omega )={\overline { {\widehat {f} }(\omega )} }\, \quad ; \quad {\widehat {f} }(-\omega )={\overline { {\widehat {f} }(\omega )} }\,$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,364!2025-12-22,39,290-->
>   - \(110\) For _f_\(_x_\) purely real: ${\widehat {f} }(-\xi )={\overline { {\widehat {f} }(\xi )} }\,$ :@: Hermitian symmetry. _z_ indicates the [complex conjugate](complex%20conjugate.md). <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,345-->
> - \(113\) For _f_\(_x_\) purely imaginary ::@:: ${\widehat {f} }(-\xi )=-{\overline { {\widehat {f} }(\xi )} }\, \quad ; \quad {\widehat {f} }(-\omega )=-{\overline { {\widehat {f} }(\omega )} }\, \quad ; \quad {\widehat {f} }(-\omega )=-{\overline { {\widehat {f} }(\omega )} }\,$ <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,350!2025-12-01,19,365-->
>   - \(113\) For _f_\(_x_\) purely imaginary: ${\widehat {f} }(-\xi )=-{\overline { {\widehat {f} }(\xi )} }\,$ :@: _z_ indicates the [complex conjugate](complex%20conjugate.md). <!--SR:!2025-11-28,16,324-->
> - \(114\) ${\overline {f(x)} }$ ::@:: ${\overline { {\widehat {f} }(-\xi )} } \quad ; \quad {\overline { {\widehat {f} }(-\omega )} } \quad ; \quad {\overline { {\widehat {f} }(-\omega )} }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,349!2025-11-29,17,355-->
>   - \(114\) ${\overline {f(x)} } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\overline { {\widehat {f} }(-\xi )} }$ :@: [Complex conjugation](complex%20conjugate.md), generalization of 110 and 113 <!--SR:!2025-11-28,16,333-->
> - \(115\) $f(x)\cos(ax)$ ::@:: ${\frac { {\widehat {f} }\left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)+{\widehat {f} }\left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2} } \quad ; \quad {\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\omega -a)+{\widehat {f} }(\omega +a)}{2} }\, \quad ; \quad {\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\omega -a)+{\widehat {f} }(\omega +a)}{2} }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,363!2025-11-30,18,363-->
>   - \(115\) $f(x)\cos(ax) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac { {\widehat {f} }\left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)+{\widehat {f} }\left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2} }$ :@: This follows from rules 101 and 103 using [Euler's formula](Euler's%20formula.md): <br/> $\cos(ax)={\frac {e^{iax}+e^{-iax} }{2} }$. <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,355-->
> - \(116\) $f(x)\sin(ax)$ ::@:: ${\frac { {\widehat {f} }\left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)-{\widehat {f} }\left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2i} } \quad ; \quad {\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\omega -a)-{\widehat {f} }(\omega +a)}{2i} } \quad ; \quad {\frac { {\widehat {f} }(\omega -a)-{\widehat {f} }(\omega +a)}{2i} }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361!2025-11-29,17,353-->
>   - \(116\) $f(x)\sin(ax) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac { {\widehat {f} }\left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)-{\widehat {f} }\left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2i} }$ :@: This follows from 101 and 103 using [Euler's formula](Euler's%20formula.md): <br/> $\sin(ax)={\frac {e^{iax}-e^{-iax} }{2i} }$. <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,348-->

### square-integrable functions, one-dimensional

The Fourier transforms in this table may be found in [Campbell & Foster \(1948\)](#CITEREFCampbellFoster1948), [Erdélyi \(1954\)](#CITEREFErd%C3%A9lyi1954), or [Kammler \(2000](#CITEREFKammler2000), appendix\).

|     | Function                                     | Fourier transform <br/> unitary, ordinary frequency                                                                                               | Fourier transform <br/> unitary, angular frequency                                                                                                                                | Fourier transform <br/> non-unitary, angular frequency                                                                                                | Remarks                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| --- | -------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|     | $f(x)\,$                                     | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\xi )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{1}(\xi )\\&=\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i2\pi \xi x}\,dx\end{aligned} }$ | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{2}(\omega )\\&={\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i\omega x}\,dx\end{aligned} }$ | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{3}(\omega )\\&=\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i\omega x}\,dx\end{aligned} }$ | Definitions                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 201 | $\operatorname {rect} (ax)\,$                | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }\,\operatorname {sinc}_\pi \left({\frac {\xi }{a} }\right)$                                                         | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi a^{2} } } }\,\operatorname {sinc}_\pi \left({\frac {\omega }{2\pi a} }\right)$                                                                            | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }\,\operatorname {sinc}_\pi \left({\frac {\omega }{2\pi a} }\right)$                                                     | The [rectangular pulse](rectangular%20function.md) and the _normalized_ [sinc function](sinc%20function.md), here defined as sinc\(_x_\) = ⁠sin\(π<!-- markdown separator -->_x_\)/π<!-- markdown separator -->_x_⁠                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| 202 | $\operatorname {sinc_\pi} (ax)\,$            | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }\,\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\xi }{a} }\right)\,$                                                           | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi a^{2} } } }\,\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2\pi a} }\right)$                                                                                | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }\,\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2\pi a} }\right)$                                                         | Dual of rule 201. The [rectangular function](rectangular%20function.md) is an ideal [low-pass filter](low-pass%20filter.md), and the [sinc function](sinc%20function.md) is the [non-causal](anticausal%20system.md) impulse response of such a filter. The [sinc function](sinc%20function.md) is defined here as sinc\(_x_\) = ⁠sin\(π<!-- markdown separator -->_x_\)/π<!-- markdown separator -->_x_⁠                   |
| 203 | $\operatorname {sinc}_\pi ^{2}(ax)$          | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }\,\operatorname {tri} \left({\frac {\xi }{a} }\right)$                                                              | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi a^{2} } } }\,\operatorname {tri} \left({\frac {\omega }{2\pi a} }\right)$                                                                                 | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }\,\operatorname {tri} \left({\frac {\omega }{2\pi a} }\right)$                                                          | The function tri\(_x_\) is the [triangular function](triangular%20function.md)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| 204 | $\operatorname {tri} (ax)$                   | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }\,\operatorname {sinc}_\pi ^{2}\left({\frac {\xi }{a} }\right)\,$                                                   | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi a^{2} } } }\,\operatorname {sinc}_\pi ^{2}\left({\frac {\omega }{2\pi a} }\right)$                                                                        | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }\,\operatorname {sinc}_\pi ^{2}\left({\frac {\omega }{2\pi a} }\right)$                                                 | Dual of rule 203.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| 205 | $e^{-ax}u(x)\,$                              | ${\frac {1}{a+i2\pi \xi } }$                                                                                                                      | ${\frac {1}{ {\sqrt {2\pi } }(a+i\omega )} }$                                                                                                                                     | ${\frac {1}{a+i\omega } }$                                                                                                                            | The function _u_\(_x_\) is the [Heaviside unit step function](Heaviside%20step%20function.md) and _a_ \> 0.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 206 | $e^{-\alpha x^{2} }\,$                       | ${\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{\alpha } } }\,e^{-{\frac {(\pi \xi )^{2} }{\alpha } } }$                                                                    | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\alpha } } }\,e^{-{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4\alpha } } }$                                                                                                        | ${\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{\alpha } } }\,e^{-{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4\alpha } } }$                                                                          | This shows that, for the unitary Fourier transforms, the [Gaussian function](Gaussian%20function.md) _e_<sup>−<!-- markdown separator -->_αx_<sup>2</sup></sup> is its own Fourier transform for some choice of _α_. For this to be integrable we must have Re\(_α_\) \> 0.                                                                                                                                                 |
| 208 | $e^{-a \lvert x \rvert}\,$                   | ${\frac {2a}{a^{2}+4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } }$                                                                                                         | ${\sqrt {\frac {2}{\pi } } }\,{\frac {a}{a^{2}+\omega ^{2} } }$                                                                                                                   | ${\frac {2a}{a^{2}+\omega ^{2} } }$                                                                                                                   | For Re\(_a_\) \> 0. That is, the Fourier transform of a [two-sided decaying exponential function](laplace%20distribution.md) is a [Lorentzian function](Lorentzian%20function.md#Probability%20density%20function%20(PDF)).                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 209 | $\operatorname {sech} (ax)\,$                | ${\frac {\pi }{\lvert a \rvert} }\operatorname {sech} \left({\frac {\pi ^{2} }{a} }\xi \right)$                                                   | ${\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }\operatorname {sech} \left({\frac {\pi }{2a} }\omega \right)$                                                            | ${\frac {\pi }{\lvert a \rvert} }\operatorname {sech} \left({\frac {\pi }{2a} }\omega \right)$                                                        | [Hyperbolic secant](hyperbolic%20function.md) is its own Fourier transform                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| 210 | $e^{-{\frac {a^{2}x^{2} }{2} } }H_{n}(ax)\,$ | ${\frac { {\sqrt {2\pi } }(-i)^{n} }{a} }e^{-{\frac {2\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a^{2} } } }H_{n}\left({\frac {2\pi \xi }{a} }\right)$                    | ${\frac {(-i)^{n} }{a} }e^{-{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{2a^{2} } } }H_{n}\left({\frac {\omega }{a} }\right)$                                                                            | ${\frac {(-i)^{n}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }{a} }e^{-{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{2a^{2} } } }H_{n}\left({\frac {\omega }{a} }\right)$                                | _H<sub>n</sub>_ is the _n_<!-- markdown separator -->th-order [Hermite polynomial](Hermite%20polynomial.md). If _a_ = 1 then the Gauss–Hermite functions are [eigenfunctions](eigenfunction.md) of the Fourier transform operator. For a derivation, see [Hermite polynomial](Hermite%20polynomials.md#Hermite%20functions%20as%20eigenfunctions%20of%20the%20Fourier%20transform). The formula reduces to 206 for _n_ = 0. |

> - \(205\) $e^{-ax}u(x)\,$ ::@:: ${\frac {1}{a+i2\pi \xi } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{ {\sqrt {2\pi } }(a+i\omega )} } \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{a+i\omega } }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,349!2025-12-02,20,361-->

>   - \(205\) $e^{-ax}u(x)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{a+i2\pi \xi } }$ / mnemonic ::@:: Integrate at zero frequency to get $\frac 1 a$. Then simply add $i 2\pi \xi$ to the denominator. <p> Alternatively, integrate $e^{-(a + i 2\pi \xi)x}$ over $[0, +\infty)$ directly. <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361!2026-01-23,59,336-->
> - \(206\) $e^{-\alpha x^{2} }\,$ ::@:: ${\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{\alpha } } }\,e^{-{\frac {(\pi \xi )^{2} }{\alpha } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\alpha } } }\,e^{-{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4\alpha } } } \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{\alpha } } }\,e^{-{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4\alpha } } }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,355!2025-11-30,18,338-->

For this to be integrable we must have Re\(_α_\) \> 0. <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361-->
>   - \(206\) $e^{-\alpha x^{2} }\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{\alpha } } }\,e^{-{\frac {(\pi \xi )^{2} }{\alpha } } }$ / mnemonic ::@:: Recall $e^{-\pi x^2} \stackrel {\mathcal F} \Longleftrightarrow e^{-\pi \xi^2}$ and then apply the argument scaling property. <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,338!2025-12-02,20,361-->
> - \(208\) $e^{-a \lvert x \rvert}\,$ ::@:: ${\frac {2a}{a^{2}+4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } } \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {\frac {2}{\pi } } }\,{\frac {a}{a^{2}+\omega ^{2} } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {2a}{a^{2}+\omega ^{2} } }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,364!2025-12-02,20,361-->

>   - \(208\) $e^{-a \lvert x \rvert}\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {2a}{a^{2}+4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } }$ / mnemonic ::@:: Add the Fourier transforms of $f(x) = e^{-ax}u(x)$ and $f(-x) = e^{ax}u(-x)$. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,338!2025-11-30,18,359-->
> - \(209\) $\operatorname {sech} (ax)\,$ ::@:: ${\frac {\pi }{\lvert a \rvert} }\operatorname {sech} \left({\frac {\pi ^{2} }{a} }\xi \right) \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\lvert a \rvert} }{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }\operatorname {sech} \left({\frac {\pi }{2a} }\omega \right) \quad ; \quad {\frac {\pi }{\lvert a \rvert} }\operatorname {sech} \left({\frac {\pi }{2a} }\omega \right)$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-11-28,16,336-->
>   - \(209\) $\operatorname {sech} (ax)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {\pi }{\lvert a \rvert} }\operatorname {sech} \left({\frac {\pi ^{2} }{a} }\xi \right)$ :@: [Hyperbolic secant](hyperbolic%20function.md) is its own Fourier transform <!--SR:!2025-11-28,16,324-->
>   - \(209\) $\operatorname {sech} (ax)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {\pi }{\lvert a \rvert} }\operatorname {sech} \left({\frac {\pi ^{2} }{a} }\xi \right)$/ mnemonic ::@:: Recall $\operatorname{sech}(\pi x) \stackrel {\mathcal F} \Longleftrightarrow \operatorname{sech}(\pi x)$ and then apply the argument scaling property. <!--SR:!2026-02-03,68,334!2025-11-29,17,355-->
> - \(210\) $e^{-{\frac {a^{2}x^{2} }{2} } }H_{n}(ax)\,$ ::@:: ${\frac { {\sqrt {2\pi } }(-i)^{n} }{a} }e^{-{\frac {2\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a^{2} } } }H_{n}\left({\frac {2\pi \xi }{a} }\right) \quad ; \quad {\frac {(-i)^{n} }{a} }e^{-{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{2a^{2} } } }H_{n}\left({\frac {\omega }{a} }\right) \quad ; \quad {\frac {(-i)^{n}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }{a} }e^{-{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{2a^{2} } } }H_{n}\left({\frac {\omega }{a} }\right)$ <!--SR:!2026-01-22,58,338!2026-01-09,46,290-->
>   - \(210\) $e^{-{\frac {a^{2}x^{2} }{2} } }H_{n}(ax)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac { {\sqrt {2\pi } }(-i)^{n} }{a} }e^{-{\frac {2\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a^{2} } } }H_{n}\left({\frac {2\pi \xi }{a} }\right)$ :@: _H<sub>n</sub>_ is the _n_<!-- markdown separator -->th-order [Hermite polynomial](Hermite%20polynomial.md). If _a_ = 1 then the Gauss–Hermite functions are [eigenfunctions](eigenfunction.md) of the Fourier transform operator. For a derivation, see [Hermite polynomial](Hermite%20polynomials.md#Hermite%20functions%20as%20eigenfunctions%20of%20the%20Fourier%20transform). The formula reduces to 206 for _n_ = 0. <!--SR:!2026-01-20,56,324-->
>   - \(210\) $e^{-{\frac {a^{2}x^{2} }{2} } }H_{n}(ax)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac { {\sqrt {2\pi } }(-i)^{n} }{a} }e^{-{\frac {2\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a^{2} } } }H_{n}\left({\frac {2\pi \xi }{a} }\right)$ / mnemonic ::@:: Recall $e^{- {\pi x^{2} } }H_{n}(\sqrt{2\pi} x)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } (-i)^{n} e^{- {\pi \xi ^{2} } }H_{n}\left({\sqrt{2\pi} \xi }\right)$ and then apply the argument scaling property. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,355!2025-12-02,20,364-->

### distributions, one-dimensional

The Fourier transforms in this table may be found in [Erdélyi \(1954\)](#CITEREFErd%C3%A9lyi1954) or [Kammler \(2000](#CITEREFKammler2000), appendix\).

|     | Function                                                                                                                                | Fourier transform <br/> unitary, ordinary frequency                                                                                               | Fourier transform <br/> unitary, angular frequency                                                                                                                                | Fourier transform <br/> non-unitary, angular frequency                                                                                                | Remarks                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| --- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|     | $f(x)\,$                                                                                                                                | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\xi )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{1}(\xi )\\&=\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i2\pi \xi x}\,dx\end{aligned} }$ | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{2}(\omega )\\&={\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i\omega x}\,dx\end{aligned} }$ | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{3}(\omega )\\&=\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i\omega x}\,dx\end{aligned} }$ | Definitions                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| 301 | $1$                                                                                                                                     | $\delta (\xi )$                                                                                                                                   | ${\sqrt {2\pi } }\,\delta (\omega )$                                                                                                                                              | $2\pi \delta (\omega )$                                                                                                                               | The distribution _δ_\(_ξ_\) denotes the [Dirac delta function](Dirac%20delta%20function.md).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| 302 | $\delta (x)\,$                                                                                                                          | $1$                                                                                                                                               | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }\,$                                                                                                                                                  | $1$                                                                                                                                                   | Dual of rule 301.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| 303 | $e^{iax}$                                                                                                                               | $\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)$                                                                                                    | ${\sqrt {2\pi } }\,\delta (\omega -a)$                                                                                                                                            | $2\pi \delta (\omega -a)$                                                                                                                             | This follows from 103 and 301.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| 304 | $\cos(ax)$                                                                                                                              | ${\frac {\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)+\delta \left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2} }$                                         | ${\sqrt {2\pi } }\,{\frac {\delta (\omega -a)+\delta (\omega +a)}{2} }$                                                                                                           | $\pi \left(\delta (\omega -a)+\delta (\omega +a)\right)$                                                                                              | This follows from rules 101 and 303 using [Euler's formula](Euler's%20formula.md): <br/> $\cos(ax)={\frac {e^{iax}+e^{-iax} }{2} }$.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 305 | $\sin(ax)$                                                                                                                              | ${\frac {\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)-\delta \left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2i} }$                                        | ${\sqrt {2\pi } }\,{\frac {\delta (\omega -a)-\delta (\omega +a)}{2i} }$                                                                                                          | $-i\pi {\bigl (}\delta (\omega -a)-\delta (\omega +a){\bigr )}$                                                                                       | This follows from 101 and 303 using <br/> $\sin(ax)={\frac {e^{iax}-e^{-iax} }{2i} }$.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| 306 | $\cos \left(ax^{2}\right)$                                                                                                              | ${\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\cos \left({\frac {\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$                                                 | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {2a} } }\cos \left({\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$                                                                                       | ${\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\cos \left({\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$                                                         | This follows from 101 and 207 using <br/> $\cos(ax^{2})={\frac {e^{iax^{2} }+e^{-iax^{2} } }{2} }$.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| 307 | $\sin \left(ax^{2}\right)$                                                                                                              | $-{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\sin \left({\frac {\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$                                                | ${\frac {-1}{\sqrt {2a} } }\sin \left({\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$                                                                                      | $-{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\sin \left({\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$                                                        | This follows from 101 and 207 using <br/> $\sin(ax^{2})={\frac {e^{iax^{2} }-e^{-iax^{2} } }{2i} }$.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 308 | $e^{-\pi i\alpha x^{2} }\,$                                                                                                             | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\alpha } } }\,e^{-i{\frac {\pi }{4} } }e^{i{\frac {\pi \xi ^{2} }{\alpha } } }$                                                | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi \alpha } } }\,e^{-i{\frac {\pi }{4} } }e^{i{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4\pi \alpha } } }$                                                                       | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\alpha } } }\,e^{-i{\frac {\pi }{4} } }e^{i{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4\pi \alpha } } }$                                                | Here it is assumed $\alpha$ is real. For the case that alpha is complex see table entry 206 above.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| 309 | $x^{n}\,$                                                                                                                               | $\left({\frac {i}{2\pi } }\right)^{n}\delta ^{(n)}(\xi )$                                                                                         | $i^{n}{\sqrt {2\pi } }\delta ^{(n)}(\omega )$                                                                                                                                     | $2\pi i^{n}\delta ^{(n)}(\omega )$                                                                                                                    | Here, _n_ is a [natural number](natural%20number.md) and _δ_<sup>\(_n_\)</sup>\(_ξ_\) is the _n_<!-- markdown separator -->th distribution derivative of the Dirac delta function. This rule follows from rules 107 and 301. Combining this rule with 101, we can transform all [polynomials](polynomial.md).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| 310 | $\delta ^{(n)}(x)$                                                                                                                      | $(i2\pi \xi )^{n}$                                                                                                                                | ${\frac {(i\omega )^{n} }{\sqrt {2\pi } } }$                                                                                                                                      | $(i\omega )^{n}$                                                                                                                                      | Dual of rule 309. _δ_<sup>\(_n_\)</sup>\(_ξ_\) is the _n_<!-- markdown separator -->th distribution derivative of the Dirac delta function. This rule follows from 106 and 302.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| 311 | ${\frac {1}{x} }$                                                                                                                       | $-i\pi \operatorname {sgn}(\xi )$                                                                                                                 | $-i{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }\operatorname {sgn}(\omega )$                                                                                                                       | $-i\pi \operatorname {sgn}(\omega )$                                                                                                                  | Here sgn\(_ξ_\) is the [sign function](sign%20function.md). Note that ⁠1/_x_⁠ is not a distribution. It is necessary to use the [Cauchy principal value](Cauchy%20principal%20value.md) when testing against [Schwartz functions](Schwartz%20functions.md). This rule is useful in studying the [Hilbert transform](hilbert%20transform.md).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| 312 | ${\begin{aligned}&{\frac {1}{x^{n} } }\\&:={\frac {(-1)^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }{\frac {d^{n} }{dx^{n} } }\log \lvert x \rvert\end{aligned} }$ | $-i\pi {\frac {(-i2\pi \xi )^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }\operatorname {sgn}(\xi )$                                                                          | $-i{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }\,{\frac {(-i\omega )^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }\operatorname {sgn}(\omega )$                                                                                | $-i\pi {\frac {(-i\omega )^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }\operatorname {sgn}(\omega )$                                                                             | ⁠1/_x_<sup>_n_</sup>⁠ is the [homogeneous distribution](homogeneous%20distribution.md) defined by the distributional derivative <br/> ${\frac {(-1)^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }{\frac {d^{n} }{dx^{n} } }\log \lvert x \rvert$                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 313 | ${\lvert x \rvert}^{\alpha }$                                                                                                           | $-{\frac {2\sin \left({\frac {\pi \alpha }{2} }\right)\Gamma (\alpha +1)}{ {\lvert 2\pi \xi \rvert}^{\alpha +1} } }$                              | ${\frac {-2}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }\,{\frac {\sin \left({\frac {\pi \alpha }{2} }\right)\Gamma (\alpha +1)}{ {\lvert \omega \rvert}^{\alpha +1} } }$                                   | $-{\frac {2\sin \left({\frac {\pi \alpha }{2} }\right)\Gamma (\alpha +1)}{ {\lvert \omega \rvert}^{\alpha +1} } }$                                    | This formula is valid for 0 \> _α_ \> −1. For _α_ \> 0 some singular terms arise at the origin that can be found by differentiating 320. If Re _α_ \> −1, then &vert;_x_&vert;<sup>_α_</sup> is a locally integrable function, and so a tempered distribution. The function _α_ ↦ &vert;_x_&vert;<sup>_α_</sup> is a holomorphic function from the right half-plane to the space of tempered distributions. It admits a unique meromorphic extension to a tempered distribution, also denoted &vert;_x_&vert;<sup>_α_</sup> for _α_ ≠ −1, −3, ... \(See [homogeneous distribution](homogeneous%20distribution.md).\) |
|     | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\lvert x \rvert} } }$                                                                                                | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\lvert \xi \rvert} } }$                                                                                                        | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\lvert \omega \rvert} } }$                                                                                                                                     | ${\frac {\sqrt {2\pi } }{\sqrt {\lvert \omega \rvert} } }$                                                                                            | Special case of 313.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| 314 | $\operatorname {sgn}(x)$                                                                                                                | ${\frac {1}{i\pi \xi } }$                                                                                                                         | ${\sqrt {\frac {2}{\pi } } }{\frac {1}{i\omega } }$                                                                                                                               | ${\frac {2}{i\omega } }$                                                                                                                              | The dual of rule 311. This time the Fourier transforms need to be considered as a [Cauchy principal value](Cauchy%20principal%20value.md).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| 315 | $u(x)$                                                                                                                                  | ${\frac {1}{2} }\left({\frac {1}{i\pi \xi } }+\delta (\xi )\right)$                                                                               | ${\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }\left({\frac {1}{i\pi \omega } }+\delta (\omega )\right)$                                                                                             | $\pi \left({\frac {1}{i\pi \omega } }+\delta (\omega )\right)$                                                                                        | The function _u_\(_x_\) is the Heaviside [unit step function](Heaviside%20step%20function.md); this follows from rules 101, 301, and 314.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| 316 | $\sum _{n=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta (x-nT)$                                                                                             | ${\frac {1}{T} }\sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {k}{T} }\right)$                                                             | ${\frac {\sqrt {2\pi } }{T} }\sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta \left(\omega -{\frac {2\pi k}{T} }\right)$                                                                        | ${\frac {2\pi }{T} }\sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta \left(\omega -{\frac {2\pi k}{T} }\right)$                                                     | This function is known as the [Dirac comb](Dirac%20comb.md) function. This result can be derived from 302 and 102, together with the fact that <br/> ${\begin{aligned}&\sum _{n=-\infty }^{\infty }e^{inx}\\={}&2\pi \sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta (x+2\pi k)\end{aligned} }$ <br/> as distributions.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| 317 | $J_{0}(x)$                                                                                                                              | ${\frac {2\,\operatorname {rect} (\pi \xi )}{\sqrt {1-4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } } }$                                                                    | ${\sqrt {\frac {2}{\pi } } }\,{\frac {\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2} }\right)}{\sqrt {1-\omega ^{2} } } }$                                                        | ${\frac {2\,\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2} }\right)}{\sqrt {1-\omega ^{2} } } }$                                                      | The function _J_<sub>0</sub>\(_x_\) is the zeroth order [Bessel function](Bessel%20function.md) of first kind.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| 318 | $J_{n}(x)$                                                                                                                              | ${\frac {2(-i)^{n}T_{n}(2\pi \xi )\operatorname {rect} (\pi \xi )}{\sqrt {1-4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } } }$                                              | ${\sqrt {\frac {2}{\pi } } }{\frac {(-i)^{n}T_{n}(\omega )\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2} }\right)}{\sqrt {1-\omega ^{2} } } }$                                    | ${\frac {2(-i)^{n}T_{n}(\omega )\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2} }\right)}{\sqrt {1-\omega ^{2} } } }$                                  | This is a generalization of 317. The function _J<sub>n</sub>_\(_x_\) is the _n_<!-- markdown separator -->th order [Bessel function](Bessel%20function.md) of first kind. The function _T<sub>n</sub>_\(_x_\) is the [Chebyshev polynomial of the first kind](Chebyshev%20polynomials.md).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| 319 | $\log \left\lvert{x} \right\rvert$                                                                                                      | $-{\frac {1}{2} }{\frac {1}{\left\lvert\xi \right\rvert} }-\gamma \delta \left(\xi \right)$                                                       | $-{\frac {\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }{\left\lvert\omega \right\rvert} }-{\sqrt {2\pi } }\gamma \delta \left(\omega \right)$                                                        | $-{\frac {\pi }{\left\lvert\omega \right\rvert} }-2\pi \gamma \delta \left(\omega \right)$                                                            | _γ_ is the [Euler–Mascheroni constant](Euler–Mascheroni%20constant.md). It is necessary to use a finite part integral when testing ⁠1/&vert;_ξ_&vert;⁠ or ⁠1/&vert;_ω_&vert; ⁠against [Schwartz functions](Schwartz%20functions.md). The details of this might change the coefficient of the delta function.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| 320 | $\left(\mp ix\right)^{-\alpha }$                                                                                                        | ${\frac {\left(2\pi \right)^{\alpha } }{\Gamma \left(\alpha \right)} }u\left(\pm \xi \right)\left(\pm \xi \right)^{\alpha -1}$                    | ${\frac {\sqrt {2\pi } }{\Gamma \left(\alpha \right)} }u\left(\pm \omega \right)\left(\pm \omega \right)^{\alpha -1}$                                                             | ${\frac {2\pi }{\Gamma \left(\alpha \right)} }u\left(\pm \omega \right)\left(\pm \omega \right)^{\alpha -1}$                                          | This formula is valid for 1 \> _α_ \> 0. Use differentiation to derive formula for higher exponents. _u_ is the Heaviside function.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |

> __flashcards__
>
> - \(def\) $f(x)\,$ <!-- flashcard ID: 85021938-f8d8-4d2e-9bef-af71c310be7d -->::@:: ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\xi )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{1}(\xi )\\&=\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i2\pi \xi x}\,dx\end{aligned} } \quad ; \quad {\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{2}(\omega )\\&={\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i\omega x}\,dx\end{aligned} } \quad ; \quad {\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{3}(\omega )\\&=\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i\omega x}\,dx\end{aligned} }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,365!2025-12-02,20,365-->
>   - \(def\) $f(x)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\xi )\triangleq {\widehat {f} }_{1}(\xi )\\&=\int _{-\infty }^{\infty }f(x)e^{-i2\pi \xi x}\,dx\end{aligned} }$ <!-- flashcard ID: 19b220dc-45c2-4cba-a0e8-909ecf9a61c0 -->:@: Definitions <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,349-->
> - \(301\) $1$ ::@:: $\delta (\xi ) \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {2\pi } }\,\delta (\omega ) \quad ; \quad 2\pi \delta (\omega )$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,355!2026-01-20,56,324-->
>   - \(301\) $1 {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } \delta (\xi )$ :@: The distribution _δ_\(_ξ_\) denotes the [Dirac delta function](Dirac%20delta%20function.md). <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,355-->
> - \(302\) $\delta (x)\,$ ::@:: $1 \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }\, \quad ; \quad 1$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,355!2025-12-02,20,361-->
>   - \(302\) $\delta (x)\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } 1$ :@: Dual of rule 301. <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,359-->
> - \(303\) $e^{iax}$ ::@:: $\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right) \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {2\pi } }\,\delta (\omega -a) \quad ; \quad 2\pi \delta (\omega -a)$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361!2025-12-02,20,363-->
>   - \(303\) $e^{iax} {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } \delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)$ :@: This follows from 103 and 301. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,358-->
>   - \(303\) $e^{iax} {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } \delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)$ / mnemonic ::@:: Simply think of the frequencies of $e^{iax}$. <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-12-02,20,358-->
> - \(304\) $\cos(ax)$ ::@:: ${\frac {\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)+\delta \left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2} } \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {2\pi } }\,{\frac {\delta (\omega -a)+\delta (\omega +a)}{2} } \quad ; \quad \pi \left(\delta (\omega -a)+\delta (\omega +a)\right)$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,364!2025-11-29,17,349-->
>   - \(304\) $\cos(ax) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)+\delta \left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2} }$ :@: This follows from rules 101 and 303 using [Euler's formula](Euler's%20formula.md): <br/> $\cos(ax)={\frac {e^{iax}+e^{-iax} }{2} }$. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,363-->
> - \(305\) $\sin(ax)$ ::@:: ${\frac {\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)-\delta \left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2i} } \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {2\pi } }\,{\frac {\delta (\omega -a)-\delta (\omega +a)}{2i} } \quad ; \quad -i\pi {\bigl (}\delta (\omega -a)-\delta (\omega +a){\bigr )}$ <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,355!2025-12-01,19,353-->
>   - \(305\) $\sin(ax) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)-\delta \left(\xi +{\frac {a}{2\pi } }\right)}{2i} }$ :@: This follows from 101 and 303 using <br/> $\sin(ax)={\frac {e^{iax}-e^{-iax} }{2i} }$. <!--SR:!2026-02-03,68,334-->
> - \(306\) $\cos \left(ax^{2}\right)$ ::@:: ${\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\cos \left({\frac {\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right) \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\sqrt {2a} } }\cos \left({\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right) \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\cos \left({\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$ <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,350!2026-01-20,56,317-->
>   - \(306\) $\cos \left(ax^{2}\right) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\cos \left({\frac {\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$ :@: This follows from 101 and 207 using <br/> $\cos(ax^{2})={\frac {e^{iax^{2} }+e^{-iax^{2} } }{2} }$. <!--SR:!2026-01-24,60,349-->
>   - \(306\) $\cos \left(ax^{2}\right) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\cos \left({\frac {\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$ / mnemonic ::@:: Recall $\cos \left(\pi x^{2}\right) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } \cos \left({\pi \xi ^{2} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$ and then apply the argument scaling property. <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,338!2025-11-30,18,363-->
> - \(307\) $\sin \left(ax^{2}\right)$ ::@:: $-{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\sin \left({\frac {\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right) \quad ; \quad {\frac {-1}{\sqrt {2a} } }\sin \left({\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right) \quad ; \quad -{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\sin \left({\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$ <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,359!2025-12-02,20,359-->
>   - \(307\) $\sin \left(ax^{2}\right) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } -{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\sin \left({\frac {\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$ :@: This follows from 101 and 207 using <br/> $\sin(ax^{2})={\frac {e^{iax^{2} }-e^{-iax^{2} } }{2i} }$. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,350-->
>   - \(307\) $\sin \left(ax^{2}\right) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } -{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{a} } }\sin \left({\frac {\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} }{a} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$ / mnemonic ::@:: Recall $\sin \left(\pi x^{2}\right) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } -\sin \left({\pi \xi ^{2} }-{\frac {\pi }{4} }\right)$ and then apply the argument scaling property. <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-12-01,19,364-->
> - \(308\) $e^{-\pi i\alpha x^{2} }\,$ ::@:: ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\alpha } } }\,e^{-i{\frac {\pi }{4} } }e^{i{\frac {\pi \xi ^{2} }{\alpha } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\sqrt {2\pi \alpha } } }\,e^{-i{\frac {\pi }{4} } }e^{i{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4\pi \alpha } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\sqrt {\alpha } } }\,e^{-i{\frac {\pi }{4} } }e^{i{\frac {\omega ^{2} }{4\pi \alpha } } }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,359!2026-01-21,57,324-->
>   - \(308\) $e^{-\pi i\alpha x^{2} }\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{\sqrt {\alpha } } }\,e^{-i{\frac {\pi }{4} } }e^{i{\frac {\pi \xi ^{2} }{\alpha } } }$ :@: Here it is assumed $\alpha$ is real. For the case that alpha is complex see table entry 206 above. <!--SR:!2026-01-21,57,338-->
>   - \(308\) $e^{-\pi i\alpha x^{2} }\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{\sqrt {\alpha } } }\,e^{-i{\frac {\pi }{4} } }e^{i{\frac {\pi \xi ^{2} }{\alpha } } }$ / mnemonic ::@:: Recall $e^{-i \pi x^{2} }\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } e^{i {\pi \left(\xi ^{2} - \frac 1 4\right) } }$ and then apply the argument scaling property.  <p> Alternatively, the above can be recalled using $e^{-\pi x^2} \stackrel {\mathcal F} {\Longleftrightarrow} e^{-\pi x^2}$ and then apply the argument scaling property with $a = \sqrt i = e^{-i \frac \pi 4}$. <!--SR:!2025-11-28,16,333!2025-12-02,20,361-->
> - \(309\) $x^{n}\,$ ::@:: $\left({\frac {i}{2\pi } }\right)^{n}\delta ^{(n)}(\xi ) \quad ; \quad i^{n}{\sqrt {2\pi } }\delta ^{(n)}(\omega ) \quad ; \quad 2\pi i^{n}\delta ^{(n)}(\omega )$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,355!2025-11-28,16,333-->
>   - \(309\) $x^{n}\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } \left({\frac {i}{2\pi } }\right)^{n}\delta ^{(n)}(\xi )$ :@: Here, _n_ is a [natural number](natural%20number.md) and _δ_<sup>\(_n_\)</sup>\(_ξ_\) is the _n_<!-- markdown separator -->th distribution derivative of the Dirac delta function. This rule follows from rules 107 and 301. Combining this rule with 101, we can transform all [polynomials](polynomial.md). <!--SR:!2026-01-21,57,324-->
> - \(310\) $\delta ^{(n)}(x)$ ::@:: $(i2\pi \xi )^{n} \quad ; \quad {\frac {(i\omega )^{n} }{\sqrt {2\pi } } } \quad ; \quad (i\omega )^{n}$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,363!2025-11-30,18,338-->
>   - \(310\) $\delta ^{(n)}(x) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } (i2\pi \xi )^{n}$ :@: Dual of rule 309. _δ_<sup>\(_n_\)</sup>\(_ξ_\) is the _n_<!-- markdown separator -->th distribution derivative of the Dirac delta function. This rule follows from 106 and 302. <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,355-->
> - \(311\) ${\frac {1}{x} }$ ::@:: $-i\pi \operatorname {sgn}(\xi ) \quad ; \quad -i{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }\operatorname {sgn}(\omega ) \quad ; \quad -i\pi \operatorname {sgn}(\omega )$ <!--SR:!2025-12-17,27,330!2025-12-01,19,350-->
>   - \(311\) ${\frac {1}{x} } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } -i\pi \operatorname {sgn}(\xi )$ :@: Here sgn\(_ξ_\) is the [sign function](sign%20function.md). Note that ⁠1/_x_⁠ is not a distribution. It is necessary to use the [Cauchy principal value](Cauchy%20principal%20value.md) when testing against [Schwartz functions](Schwartz%20functions.md). This rule is useful in studying the [Hilbert transform](hilbert%20transform.md). <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,349-->
> - \(312\) ${\begin{aligned}&{\frac {1}{x^{n} } }\\&:={\frac {(-1)^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }{\frac {d^{n} }{dx^{n} } }\log \lvert x \rvert\end{aligned} }$ ::@:: $-i\pi {\frac {(-i2\pi \xi )^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }\operatorname {sgn}(\xi ) \quad ; \quad -i{\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }\,{\frac {(-i\omega )^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }\operatorname {sgn}(\omega ) \quad ; \quad -i\pi {\frac {(-i\omega )^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }\operatorname {sgn}(\omega )$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-11-29,17,318-->
>   - \(312\) ${\begin{aligned}&{\frac {1}{x^{n} } }\\&:={\frac {(-1)^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }{\frac {d^{n} }{dx^{n} } }\log \lvert x \rvert\end{aligned} } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } -i\pi {\frac {(-i2\pi \xi )^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }\operatorname {sgn}(\xi )$ :@: ⁠1/_x_<sup>_n_</sup>⁠ is the [homogeneous distribution](homogeneous%20distribution.md) defined by the distributional derivative <br/> ${\frac {(-1)^{n-1} }{(n-1)!} }{\frac {d^{n} }{dx^{n} } }\log \lvert x \rvert$ <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,355-->
> - \(313\) ${\lvert x \rvert}^{\alpha }$ ::@:: $-{\frac {2\sin \left({\frac {\pi \alpha }{2} }\right)\Gamma (\alpha +1)}{ {\lvert 2\pi \xi \rvert}^{\alpha +1} } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {-2}{\sqrt {2\pi } } }\,{\frac {\sin \left({\frac {\pi \alpha }{2} }\right)\Gamma (\alpha +1)}{ {\lvert \omega \rvert}^{\alpha +1} } } \quad ; \quad -{\frac {2\sin \left({\frac {\pi \alpha }{2} }\right)\Gamma (\alpha +1)}{ {\lvert \omega \rvert}^{\alpha +1} } }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,363!2025-12-30,39,341-->
>   - \(313\) ${\lvert x \rvert}^{\alpha } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } -{\frac {2\sin \left({\frac {\pi \alpha }{2} }\right)\Gamma (\alpha +1)}{ {\lvert 2\pi \xi \rvert}^{\alpha +1} } }$ :@: This formula is valid for 0 \> _α_ \> −1. For _α_ \> 0 some singular terms arise at the origin that can be found by differentiating 320. If Re _α_ \> −1, then &vert;_x_&vert;<sup>_α_</sup> is a locally integrable function, and so a tempered distribution. The function _α_ ↦ &vert;_x_&vert;<sup>_α_</sup> is a holomorphic function from the right half-plane to the space of tempered distributions. It admits a unique meromorphic extension to a tempered distribution, also denoted &vert;_x_&vert;<sup>_α_</sup> for _α_ ≠ −1, −3, ... \(See [homogeneous distribution](homogeneous%20distribution.md).\) <!--SR:!2026-01-10,46,343-->
> - \(313: special case\) ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\lvert x \rvert} } }$ ::@:: ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\lvert \xi \rvert} } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\sqrt {\lvert \omega \rvert} } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {\sqrt {2\pi } }{\sqrt {\lvert \omega \rvert} } }$ <!--SR:!2026-01-11,45,307!2025-11-30,18,349-->
>   - \(313: special case\) ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\lvert x \rvert} } } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{\sqrt {\lvert \xi \rvert} } }$ :@: Special case of 313. <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,338-->
> - \(314\) $\operatorname {sgn}(x)$ ::@:: ${\frac {1}{i\pi \xi } } \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {\frac {2}{\pi } } }{\frac {1}{i\omega } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {2}{i\omega } }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,365!2025-11-28,16,318-->
>   - \(314\) $\operatorname {sgn}(x) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{i\pi \xi } }$ :@: The dual of rule 311. This time the Fourier transforms need to be considered as a [Cauchy principal value](Cauchy%20principal%20value.md). <!--SR:!2026-01-25,61,348-->
> - \(315\) $u(x)$ ::@:: ${\frac {1}{2} }\left({\frac {1}{i\pi \xi } }+\delta (\xi )\right) \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }\left({\frac {1}{i\pi \omega } }+\delta (\omega )\right) \quad ; \quad \pi \left({\frac {1}{i\pi \omega } }+\delta (\omega )\right)$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-12-01,19,338-->
>   - \(315\) $u(x) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{2} }\left({\frac {1}{i\pi \xi } }+\delta (\xi )\right)$ :@: The function _u_\(_x_\) is the Heaviside [unit step function](Heaviside%20step%20function.md); this follows from rules 101, 301, and 314. <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,338-->
>   - \(315\) $u(x) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{2} }\left({\frac {1}{i\pi \xi } }+\delta (\xi )\right)$ / mnemonic ::@:: Add the Fourier transforms of $\operatorname{sgn}(x)$ and $1$, and then divide by 2. <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361!2025-11-29,17,355-->
> - \(316\) $\sum _{n=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta (x-nT)$ ::@:: ${\frac {1}{T} }\sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {k}{T} }\right) \quad ; \quad {\frac {\sqrt {2\pi } }{T} }\sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta \left(\omega -{\frac {2\pi k}{T} }\right) \quad ; \quad {\frac {2\pi }{T} }\sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta \left(\omega -{\frac {2\pi k}{T} }\right)$ <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,353!2025-11-30,18,355-->
>   - \(316\) $\sum _{n=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta (x-nT) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{T} }\sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {k}{T} }\right)$ :@: This function is known as the [Dirac comb](Dirac%20comb.md) function. This result can be derived from 302 and 102, together with the fact that <br/> ${\begin{aligned}&\sum _{n=-\infty }^{\infty }e^{inx}\\={}&2\pi \sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta (x+2\pi k)\end{aligned} }$ <br/> as distributions. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,353-->
>   - \(316\) $\sum _{n=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta (x-nT) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{T} }\sum _{k=-\infty }^{\infty }\delta \left(\xi -{\frac {k}{T} }\right)$ / mnemonic ::@:: If you sample \(multiplication\) the time domain every $T$ seconds, you duplicate \(convolution\) the frequency domain every $1 / T$ hertz. Additionally, remember to divide by $T$ in the frequency domain. <!--SR:!2025-11-28,16,324!2026-01-20,55,310-->
> - \(317\) $J_{0}(x)$ ::<!-- flashcard status: disabled -->@:: ${\frac {2\,\operatorname {rect} (\pi \xi )}{\sqrt {1-4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {\frac {2}{\pi } } }\,{\frac {\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2} }\right)}{\sqrt {1-\omega ^{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {2\,\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2} }\right)}{\sqrt {1-\omega ^{2} } } }$
>   - \(317\) $J_{0}(x) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {2\,\operatorname {rect} (\pi \xi )}{\sqrt {1-4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } } }$ :<!-- flashcard status: disabled -->@: The function _J_<sub>0</sub>\(_x_\) is the zeroth order [Bessel function](Bessel%20function.md) of first kind.
> - \(318\) $J_{n}(x)$ ::<!-- flashcard status: disabled -->@:: ${\frac {2(-i)^{n}T_{n}(2\pi \xi )\operatorname {rect} (\pi \xi )}{\sqrt {1-4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\sqrt {\frac {2}{\pi } } }{\frac {(-i)^{n}T_{n}(\omega )\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2} }\right)}{\sqrt {1-\omega ^{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {2(-i)^{n}T_{n}(\omega )\operatorname {rect} \left({\frac {\omega }{2} }\right)}{\sqrt {1-\omega ^{2} } } }$
>   - \(318\) $J_{n}(x) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {2(-i)^{n}T_{n}(2\pi \xi )\operatorname {rect} (\pi \xi )}{\sqrt {1-4\pi ^{2}\xi ^{2} } } }$ :<!-- flashcard status: disabled -->@: This is a generalization of 317. The function _J<sub>n</sub>_\(_x_\) is the _n_<!-- markdown separator -->th order [Bessel function](Bessel%20function.md) of first kind. The function _T<sub>n</sub>_\(_x_\) is the [Chebyshev polynomial of the first kind](Chebyshev%20polynomials.md).
> - \(319\) $\log \left\lvert{x} \right\rvert$ ::@:: $-{\frac {1}{2} }{\frac {1}{\left\lvert\xi \right\rvert} }-\gamma \delta \left(\xi \right) \quad ; \quad -{\frac {\sqrt {\frac {\pi }{2} } }{\left\lvert\omega \right\rvert} }-{\sqrt {2\pi } }\gamma \delta \left(\omega \right) \quad ; \quad -{\frac {\pi }{\left\lvert\omega \right\rvert} }-2\pi \gamma \delta \left(\omega \right)$ <!--SR:!2026-01-21,57,330!2026-01-23,59,338-->
>   - \(319\) $\log \left\lvert{x} \right\rvert {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } -{\frac {1}{2} }{\frac {1}{\left\lvert\xi \right\rvert} }-\gamma \delta \left(\xi \right)$ :@: _γ_ is the [Euler–Mascheroni constant](Euler–Mascheroni%20constant.md). It is necessary to use a finite part integral when testing ⁠1/&vert;_ξ_&vert;⁠ or ⁠1/&vert;_ω_&vert; ⁠against [Schwartz functions](Schwartz%20functions.md). The details of this might change the coefficient of the delta function. <!--SR:!2026-01-26,62,358-->
> - \(320\) $\left(\mp ix\right)^{-\alpha }$ ::@:: ${\frac {\left(2\pi \right)^{\alpha } }{\Gamma \left(\alpha \right)} }u\left(\pm \xi \right)\left(\pm \xi \right)^{\alpha -1} \quad ; \quad {\frac {\sqrt {2\pi } }{\Gamma \left(\alpha \right)} }u\left(\pm \omega \right)\left(\pm \omega \right)^{\alpha -1} \quad ; \quad {\frac {2\pi }{\Gamma \left(\alpha \right)} }u\left(\pm \omega \right)\left(\pm \omega \right)^{\alpha -1}$ <!--SR:!2025-12-04,10,270!2026-01-08,44,335-->
>   - \(320\) $\left(\mp ix\right)^{-\alpha } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {\left(2\pi \right)^{\alpha } }{\Gamma \left(\alpha \right)} }u\left(\pm \xi \right)\left(\pm \xi \right)^{\alpha -1}$ :@: This formula is valid for 1 \> _α_ \> 0. Use differentiation to derive formula for higher exponents. _u_ is the Heaviside function. <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,355-->

### two-dimensional functions

|     | Function                                                    | Fourier transform <br/> unitary, ordinary frequency                                                                                    | Fourier transform <br/> unitary, angular frequency                                                                                                               | Fourier transform <br/> non-unitary, angular frequency                                                                                        | Remarks                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| --- | ----------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| 400 | $f(x,y)$                                                    | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\xi _{x},\xi _{y})\triangleq \\&\iint f(x,y)e^{-i2\pi (\xi _{x}x+\xi _{y}y)}\,dx\,dy\end{aligned} }$ | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega _{x},\omega _{y})\triangleq \\&{\frac {1}{2\pi } }\iint f(x,y)e^{-i(\omega _{x}x+\omega _{y}y)}\,dx\,dy\end{aligned} }$ | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega _{x},\omega _{y})\triangleq \\&\iint f(x,y)e^{-i(\omega _{x}x+\omega _{y}y)}\,dx\,dy\end{aligned} }$ | The variables _ξ<sub>x</sub>_, _ξ<sub>y</sub>_, _ω<sub>x</sub>_, _ω<sub>y</sub>_ are real numbers. The integrals are taken over the entire plane.                                                                                                                                                           |
| 401 | $e^{-\pi \left(a^{2}x^{2}+b^{2}y^{2}\right)}$               | ${\frac {1}{\lvert ab \rvert} }e^{-\pi \left({\frac {\xi _{x}^{2} }{a^{2} } }+{\frac {\xi _{y}^{2} }{b^{2} } }\right)}$                | ${\frac {1}{2\pi \,\lvert ab \rvert} }e^{-{\frac {1}{4\pi } }\left({\frac {\omega _{x}^{2} }{a^{2} } }+{\frac {\omega _{y}^{2} }{b^{2} } }\right)}$              | ${\frac {1}{\lvert ab \rvert} }e^{-{\frac {1}{4\pi } }\left({\frac {\omega _{x}^{2} }{a^{2} } }+{\frac {\omega _{y}^{2} }{b^{2} } }\right)}$  | Both functions are Gaussians, which may not have unit volume.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| 402 | $\operatorname {circ} \left({\sqrt {x^{2}+y^{2} } }\right)$ | ${\frac {J_{1}\left(2\pi {\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } }\right)}{\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } } }$                         | ${\frac {J_{1}\left({\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } }\right)}{\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } } }$                                            | ${\frac {2\pi J_{1}\left({\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } }\right)}{\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } } }$                    | The function is defined by circ\(_r_\) = 1 for 0 ≤ _r_ ≤ 1, and is 0 otherwise. The result is the amplitude distribution of the [Airy disk](Airy%20disk.md), and is expressed using _J_<sub>1</sub> \(the order-1 [Bessel function](Bessel%20function.md) of the first kind\).<sup>[\[81\]](#^ref-81)</sup> |
| 403 | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {x^{2}+y^{2} } } }$                       | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } } }$                                                                                    | ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } } }$                                                                                                        | ${\frac {2\pi }{\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } } }$                                                                                 | This is the [Hankel transform](hankel%20transform.md) of _r_<sup>−1</sup>, a 2-D Fourier "self-transform".<sup>[\[82\]](#^ref-82)</sup>                                                                                                                                                                     |
| 404 | ${\frac {i}{x+iy} }$                                        | ${\frac {1}{\xi _{x}+i\xi _{y} } }$                                                                                                    | ${\frac {1}{\omega _{x}+i\omega _{y} } }$                                                                                                                        | ${\frac {2\pi }{\omega _{x}+i\omega _{y} } }$                                                                                                 | \(annotation: The input looks very similar to the output, except that the output numerator is 1 instead of _i_ \(multiply by −_i_\).\)                                                                                                                                                                      |

> - \(400\) $f(x,y)$ ::@:: ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\xi _{x},\xi _{y})\triangleq \\&\iint f(x,y)e^{-i2\pi (\xi _{x}x+\xi _{y}y)}\,dx\,dy\end{aligned} } \quad ; \quad {\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega _{x},\omega _{y})\triangleq \\&{\frac {1}{2\pi } }\iint f(x,y)e^{-i(\omega _{x}x+\omega _{y}y)}\,dx\,dy\end{aligned} } \quad ; \quad {\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }(\omega _{x},\omega _{y})\triangleq \\&\iint f(x,y)e^{-i(\omega _{x}x+\omega _{y}y)}\,dx\,dy\end{aligned} }$ <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,352!2026-01-21,57,324-->
