> - \(402\) $\operatorname {circ} \left({\sqrt {x^{2}+y^{2} } }\right)$ ::<!-- flashcard status: disabled -->@:: ${\frac {J_{1}\left(2\pi {\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } }\right)}{\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {J_{1}\left({\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } }\right)}{\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {2\pi J_{1}\left({\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } }\right)}{\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } } }$
>   - \(402\) $\operatorname {circ} \left({\sqrt {x^{2}+y^{2} } }\right) {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {J_{1}\left(2\pi {\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } }\right)}{\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } } }$ :<!-- flashcard status: disabled -->@: The function is defined by circ\(_r_\) = 1 for 0 ≤ _r_ ≤ 1, and is 0 otherwise. The result is the amplitude distribution of the [Airy disk](Airy%20disk.md), and is expressed using _J_<sub>1</sub> \(the order-1 [Bessel function](Bessel%20function.md) of the first kind\).<sup>[\[81\]](#^ref-81)</sup>
> - \(403\) ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {x^{2}+y^{2} } } }$ ::@:: ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {1}{\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {2\pi }{\sqrt {\omega _{x}^{2}+\omega _{y}^{2} } } }$ <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361!2025-11-30,18,350-->
>   - \(403\) ${\frac {1}{\sqrt {x^{2}+y^{2} } } } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{\sqrt {\xi _{x}^{2}+\xi _{y}^{2} } } }$ :@: This is the [Hankel transform](hankel%20transform.md) of _r_<sup>−1</sup>, a 2-D Fourier "self-transform".<sup>[\[82\]](#^ref-82)</sup> <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,348-->

>   - \(404\) ${\frac {i}{x+iy} } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {1}{\xi _{x}+i\xi _{y} } }$ :@: \(annotation: The input looks very similar to the output, except that the output numerator is 1 instead of _i_ \(multiply by −_i_\).\) <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,364-->

### formulas for general _n_-dimensional functions

|     | Function                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Fourier transform <br/> unitary, ordinary frequency                                                                                                                                                 | Fourier transform <br/> unitary, angular frequency                                                                                                                                                                                            | Fourier transform <br/> non-unitary, angular frequency                                                                                                                                                           | Remarks                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| --- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| 500 | $f(\mathbf {x} )\,$                                                                                                                                                                                                                | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }_{1}({\boldsymbol {\xi } })\triangleq \\&\int _{\mathbb {R} ^{n} }f(\mathbf {x} )e^{-i2\pi {\boldsymbol {\xi } }\cdot \mathbf {x} }\,d\mathbf {x} \end{aligned} }$ | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }_{2}({\boldsymbol {\omega } })\triangleq \\&{\frac {1}{ {(2\pi )}^{\frac {n}{2} } } }\int _{\mathbb {R} ^{n} }f(\mathbf {x} )e^{-i{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\cdot \mathbf {x} }\,d\mathbf {x} \end{aligned} }$ | ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }_{3}({\boldsymbol {\omega } })\triangleq \\&\int _{\mathbb {R} ^{n} }f(\mathbf {x} )e^{-i{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\cdot \mathbf {x} }\,d\mathbf {x} \end{aligned} }$             | \(annotation: definitions in general _n_ dimensions\)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| 501 | $\chi _{[0,1]}(\lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert)\left(1-{\lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\delta }$                                                                                                                                 | ${\frac {\Gamma (\delta +1)}{\pi ^{\delta }\,{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta } } }J_{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta }(2\pi \lvert{ \boldsymbol {\xi } }\rvert)$                | $2^{\delta }\,{\frac {\Gamma (\delta +1)}{\left\lvert{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\right\rvert^{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta } } }J_{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta }(\lvert{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\rvert)$                                                   | ${\frac {\Gamma (\delta +1)}{\pi ^{\delta } } }\left\lvert{\frac {\boldsymbol {\omega } }{2\pi } }\right\rvert^{-{\frac {n}{2} }-\delta }J_{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta }(\!\lvert{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\rvert\!)$ | The function _χ_<sub>\[0, 1\]</sub> is the [indicator function](indicator%20function.md) of the interval \[0, 1\]. The function Γ\(_x_\) is the gamma function. The function _J_<sub>⁠_n_/2⁠ + _δ_</sub> is a Bessel function of the first kind, with order ⁠_n_/2⁠ + _δ_. Taking _n_ = 2 and _δ_ = 0 produces 402.<sup>[\[83\]](#^ref-83)</sup>                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| 502 | ${\lvert\mathbf {x} \rvert}^{-\alpha },\quad 0<\operatorname {Re} \alpha <n.$                                                                                                                                                      | ${\frac {(2\pi )^{\alpha } }{c_{n,\alpha } } }{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{-(n-\alpha )}$                                                                                                    | ${\frac {(2\pi )^{\frac {n}{2} } }{c_{n,\alpha } } }{\lvert \boldsymbol {\omega } \rvert}^{-(n-\alpha )}$                                                                                                                                     | ${\frac {(2\pi )^{n} }{c_{n,\alpha } } }{\lvert \boldsymbol {\omega } \rvert}^{-(n-\alpha )}$                                                                                                                    | See [Riesz potential](riesz%20potential.md) where the constant is given by <br/> $c_{n,\alpha }=\pi ^{\frac {n}{2} }2^{\alpha }{\frac {\Gamma \left({\frac {\alpha }{2} }\right)}{\Gamma \left({\frac {n-\alpha }{2} }\right)} }$. <br/> The formula also holds for all _α_ ≠ _n_, _n_ + 2, ... by analytic continuation, but then the function and its Fourier transforms need to be understood as suitably regularized tempered distributions. See [homogeneous distribution](homogeneous%20distribution.md).<sup>[\[note 9\]](#^ref-note%209)</sup> |
| 503 | ${\frac {1}{\left\lvert{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }\right\rvert\left(2\pi \right)^{\frac {n}{2} } } }e^{-{\frac {1}{2} }\mathbf {x} ^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{-\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{-1}\mathbf {x} }$ | $e^{-2\pi ^{2}{\boldsymbol {\xi } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\xi } } }$                                                           | $(2\pi )^{-{\frac {n}{2} } }e^{-{\frac {1}{2} }{\boldsymbol {\omega } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\omega } } }$                                                              | $e^{-{\frac {1}{2} }{\boldsymbol {\omega } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\omega } } }$                                                            | This is the formula for a [multivariate normal distribution](multivariate%20normal%20distribution.md) normalized to 1 with a mean of 0. Bold variables are vectors or matrices. Following the notation of the aforementioned page, __Σ__ = __σ__ __σ__<sup>T</sup> and __Σ__<sup>−1</sup> = __σ__<sup>−T</sup> __σ__<sup>−1</sup>                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| 504 | $e^{-2\pi \alpha \lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert }$                                                                                                                                                                                      | ${\frac {c_{n}\alpha }{\left(\alpha ^{2}+{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } }$                                                                                       | ${\frac {c_{n}(2\pi )^{\frac {n+2}{2} }\alpha }{\left(4\pi ^{2}\alpha ^{2}+{\lvert \boldsymbol {\omega } \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } }$                                                                                            | ${\frac {c_{n}(2\pi )^{n+1}\alpha }{\left(4\pi ^{2}\alpha ^{2}+{\lvert \boldsymbol {\omega } \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } }$                                                                           | Here<sup>[\[84\]](#^ref-84)</sup> <br/> $c_{n}={\frac {\Gamma \left({\frac {n+1}{2} }\right)}{\pi ^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } }$, Re\(_α_\) \> 0                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |

> __flashcards__
>
> - \(500\) $f(\mathbf {x} )\,$ ::@:: ${\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }_{1}({\boldsymbol {\xi } })\triangleq \\&\int _{\mathbb {R} ^{n} }f(\mathbf {x} )e^{-i2\pi {\boldsymbol {\xi } }\cdot \mathbf {x} }\,d\mathbf {x} \end{aligned} } \quad ; \quad {\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }_{2}({\boldsymbol {\omega } })\triangleq \\&{\frac {1}{ {(2\pi )}^{\frac {n}{2} } } }\int _{\mathbb {R} ^{n} }f(\mathbf {x} )e^{-i{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\cdot \mathbf {x} }\,d\mathbf {x} \end{aligned} } \quad ; \quad {\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }_{3}({\boldsymbol {\omega } })\triangleq \\&\int _{\mathbb {R} ^{n} }f(\mathbf {x} )e^{-i{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\cdot \mathbf {x} }\,d\mathbf {x} \end{aligned} }$ <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,350!2025-12-02,20,359-->
>   - \(500\) $f(\mathbf {x} )\, {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\begin{aligned}&{\widehat {f} }_{1}({\boldsymbol {\xi } })\triangleq \\&\int _{\mathbb {R} ^{n} }f(\mathbf {x} )e^{-i2\pi {\boldsymbol {\xi } }\cdot \mathbf {x} }\,d\mathbf {x} \end{aligned} }$ :@: \(annotation: definitions in general _n_ dimensions\) <!--SR:!2025-12-22,39,290-->
> - \(501\) $\chi _{[0,1]}(\lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert)\left(1-{\lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\delta }$ ::<!-- flashcard status: disabled -->@:: ${\frac {\Gamma (\delta +1)}{\pi ^{\delta }\,{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta } } }J_{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta }(2\pi \lvert{ \boldsymbol {\xi } }\rvert) \quad ; \quad 2^{\delta }\,{\frac {\Gamma (\delta +1)}{\left\lvert{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\right\rvert^{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta } } }J_{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta }(\lvert{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\rvert) \quad ; \quad {\frac {\Gamma (\delta +1)}{\pi ^{\delta } } }\left\lvert{\frac {\boldsymbol {\omega } }{2\pi } }\right\rvert^{-{\frac {n}{2} }-\delta }J_{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta }(\!\lvert{\boldsymbol {\omega } }\rvert\!)$
>   - \(501\) $\chi _{[0,1]}(\lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert)\left(1-{\lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\delta } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {\Gamma (\delta +1)}{\pi ^{\delta }\,{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta } } }J_{ {\frac {n}{2} }+\delta }(2\pi \lvert{ \boldsymbol {\xi } }\rvert)$ :<!-- flashcard status: disabled -->@: The function _χ_<sub>\[0, 1\]</sub> is the [indicator function](indicator%20function.md) of the interval \[0, 1\]. The function Γ\(_x_\) is the gamma function. The function _J_<sub>⁠_n_/2⁠ + _δ_</sub> is a Bessel function of the first kind, with order ⁠_n_/2⁠ + _δ_. Taking _n_ = 2 and _δ_ = 0 produces 402.<sup>[\[83\]](#^ref-83)</sup>
> - \(502\) ${\lvert\mathbf {x} \rvert}^{-\alpha },\quad 0<\operatorname {Re} \alpha <n.$ ::@:: ${\frac {(2\pi )^{\alpha } }{c_{n,\alpha } } }{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{-(n-\alpha )} \quad ; \quad {\frac {(2\pi )^{\frac {n}{2} } }{c_{n,\alpha } } }{\lvert \boldsymbol {\omega } \rvert}^{-(n-\alpha )} \quad ; \quad {\frac {(2\pi )^{n} }{c_{n,\alpha } } }{\lvert \boldsymbol {\omega } \rvert}^{-(n-\alpha )}$ <!--SR:!2026-01-25,61,349!2025-12-04,11,253-->
>   - \(502\) ${\lvert\mathbf {x} \rvert}^{-\alpha },\quad 0<\operatorname {Re} \alpha <n. {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {(2\pi )^{\alpha } }{c_{n,\alpha } } }{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{-(n-\alpha )}$ :@: See [Riesz potential](riesz%20potential.md) where the constant is given by <br/> $c_{n,\alpha }=\pi ^{\frac {n}{2} }2^{\alpha }{\frac {\Gamma \left({\frac {\alpha }{2} }\right)}{\Gamma \left({\frac {n-\alpha }{2} }\right)} }$. <br/> The formula also holds for all _α_ ≠ _n_, _n_ + 2, ... by analytic continuation, but then the function and its Fourier transforms need to be understood as suitably regularized tempered distributions. See [homogeneous distribution](homogeneous%20distribution.md).<sup>[\[note 9\]](#^ref-note%209)</sup> <!--SR:!2026-01-09,45,330-->
>   - \(502\) ${\lvert\mathbf {x} \rvert}^{-\alpha },\quad 0<\operatorname {Re} \alpha <n. {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {(2\pi )^{\alpha } }{c_{n,\alpha } } }{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{-(n-\alpha )}$ / mnemonic ::@:: To recall $c_{n,\alpha}$ in the _denominator_, recall $\frac {\Gamma(\alpha / 2)} {\Gamma((n - \alpha) / 2)}$ first. Then add a fixed scaling factor based on the number of dimensions: $\pi^{n / 2}$. Finally add a scaling factor based on $\alpha$: $2^\alpha$. <!--SR:!2026-01-11,47,345!2025-11-30,18,365-->
> - \(503\) ${\frac {1}{\left\lvert{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }\right\rvert\left(2\pi \right)^{\frac {n}{2} } } }e^{-{\frac {1}{2} }\mathbf {x} ^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{-\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{-1}\mathbf {x} }$ ::@:: $e^{-2\pi ^{2}{\boldsymbol {\xi } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\xi } } } \quad ; \quad (2\pi )^{-{\frac {n}{2} } }e^{-{\frac {1}{2} }{\boldsymbol {\omega } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\omega } } } \quad ; \quad e^{-{\frac {1}{2} }{\boldsymbol {\omega } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\omega } } }$ <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,355!2025-11-30,18,349-->
>   - \(503\) ${\frac {1}{\left\lvert{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }\right\rvert\left(2\pi \right)^{\frac {n}{2} } } }e^{-{\frac {1}{2} }\mathbf {x} ^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{-\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{-1}\mathbf {x} } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } e^{-2\pi ^{2}{\boldsymbol {\xi } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\xi } } }$ :@: This is the formula for a [multivariate normal distribution](multivariate%20normal%20distribution.md) normalized to 1 with a mean of 0. Bold variables are vectors or matrices. Following the notation of the aforementioned page, __Σ__ = __σ__ __σ__<sup>T</sup> and __Σ__<sup>−1</sup> = __σ__<sup>−T</sup> __σ__<sup>−1</sup> <!--SR:!2026-01-04,40,318-->
>   - \(503\) ${\frac {1}{\left\lvert{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }\right\rvert\left(2\pi \right)^{\frac {n}{2} } } }e^{-{\frac {1}{2} }\mathbf {x} ^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{-\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{-1}\mathbf {x} } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } e^{-2\pi ^{2}{\boldsymbol {\xi } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }{\boldsymbol {\sigma } }^{\mathrm {T} }{\boldsymbol {\xi } } }$ / mnemonic ::@:: The function is the probability density function \(PDF\) of a multivariate normal distribution. The _non-unitary_ transform in _angular momentum_ is its characteristic function \(CF\). That CF uses the opposite sign for the exponential does not matter, as the frequency variable $\boldsymbol \sigma$ appears twice and $(-1)^2 = 1$. Then derive the other two common conventions. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,364!2025-12-02,20,361-->
> - \(504\) $e^{-2\pi \alpha \lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert }$ ::@:: ${\frac {c_{n}\alpha }{\left(\alpha ^{2}+{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {c_{n}(2\pi )^{\frac {n+2}{2} }\alpha }{\left(4\pi ^{2}\alpha ^{2}+{\lvert \boldsymbol {\omega } \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } } \quad ; \quad {\frac {c_{n}(2\pi )^{n+1}\alpha }{\left(4\pi ^{2}\alpha ^{2}+{\lvert \boldsymbol {\omega } \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } }$ <!--SR:!2026-01-10,46,335!2025-11-30,18,363-->
>   - \(504\) $e^{-2\pi \alpha \lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {c_{n}\alpha }{\left(\alpha ^{2}+{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } }$ :@: Here<sup>[\[84\]](#^ref-84)</sup> <br/> $c_{n}={\frac {\Gamma \left({\frac {n+1}{2} }\right)}{\pi ^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } }$, Re\(_α_\) \> 0 <!--SR:!2026-01-05,41,317-->
>   - \(504\) $e^{-2\pi \alpha \lvert \mathbf {x} \rvert } {\stackrel {\mathcal {F} }{\Longleftrightarrow } } {\frac {c_{n}\alpha }{\left(\alpha ^{2}+{\lvert \boldsymbol {\xi } \rvert}^{2}\right)^{\frac {n+1}{2} } } }$ / mnemonic ::@:: Recall $e^{-2\pi a \lvert x \rvert} \overset{\mathcal F} \Longleftrightarrow \frac 1 \pi \frac a {a^2 + \xi^2}$. Then generalize to _n_ dimensions by replacing $\frac 1 \pi$ with $\frac {\Gamma((n + 1) / 2)} {\pi^{(n + 1) / 2} }$ and the denominator $a^2 + \xi^2$ with $\left(a^2 + \lvert \boldsymbol \xi \rvert^2 \right)^{(n + 1) / 2}$. <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,365!2025-12-02,20,365-->

## notes

1. {@{Sentence structure}@} is often {@{sufficient to distinguish the intended meaning}@}: for example, {@{"Apply the Fourier transform to \[an input\]"}@} refers to {@{the operation}@}, whereas {@{"The Fourier transform of \[an input\]"}@} refers to {@{its output}@}. <a id="^ref-1"></a>^ref-1 <!--SR:!2025-11-30,18,338!2025-12-01,19,338!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-12-02,20,361!2025-11-28,16,333!2025-12-01,19,338-->

2. Depending on {@{the application}@} {@{a [Lebesgue integral](Lebesgue%20integral.md), [distributional](distribution%20(mathematics).md), or other approach}@} may be {@{most appropriate}@}. <a id="^ref-2"></a>^ref-2 <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,338!2025-12-01,19,358!2025-11-28,16,324-->

3. [Vretblad \(2000\)](#CITEREFVretblad2000) provides {@{solid justification for these formal procedures}@} without going too deeply into {@{[functional analysis](functional%20analysis.md) or the [theory of distributions](distribution%20(mathematics).md)}@}. <a id="^ref-3"></a>^ref-3 <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361!2025-12-01,19,355-->

4. In {@{[relativistic quantum mechanics](relativistic%20quantum%20mechanics.md)}@} one encounters {@{vector-valued Fourier transforms}@} of {@{multi-component wave functions}@}. In {@{[quantum field theory](quantum%20field%20theory.md),}@} {@{operator-valued Fourier transforms}@} of {@{operator-valued functions of spacetime}@} are {@{in frequent use}@}, see for example [Greiner & Reinhardt \(1996\)](#CITEREFGreinerReinhardt1996). <a id="^ref-4"></a>^ref-4 <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,363!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-12-02,20,363!2025-11-30,18,355!2025-11-28,16,333!2025-12-02,20,358!2025-12-01,19,345-->

5. {@{A possible source of confusion}@} is {@{the [frequency-shifting property](#frequency%20shifting)}@}; i.e. {@{the transform of function $f(x)e^{-i2\pi \xi _{0}x}$}@} is {@{${\widehat {f} }(\xi +\xi _{0})$}@}.  The value of {@{this function at  $\xi =0$}@}  is {@{${\widehat {f} }(\xi _{0})$}@}, meaning that {@{a frequency $\xi _{0}$}@} has been {@{shifted to zero}@} \(also see {@{[Negative frequency](negative%20frequency.md#simplifying%20the%20Fourier%20transform)}@}\). <a id="^ref-5"></a>^ref-5 <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,348!2025-12-01,19,338!2025-11-29,17,349!2025-12-02,20,363!2025-12-01,19,361!2025-11-29,17,350!2025-11-28,16,324!2025-11-30,18,324!2025-11-29,17,324-->

6. {@{The operator $U\left({\frac {1}{2\pi } }{\frac {d}{dx} }\right)$}@} is defined by {@{replacing $x$ by ${\frac {1}{2\pi } }{\frac {d}{dx} }$}@} in {@{the [Taylor expansion](Taylor%20series.md) of $U(x)$}@}. <a id="^ref-6"></a>^ref-6
7. Up to {@{an imaginary constant factor}@} whose {@{magnitude}@} depends on {@{what Fourier transform convention is used}@}. <a id="^ref-7"></a>^ref-7 <!--SR:!2025-12-01,19,350!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-12-02,20,363!2026-02-02,67,327!2025-12-01,19,345!2025-12-02,20,359-->

8. The direct command {@{`fourier transform of cos(6*pi*t) exp(−pi*t^2)`}@} would also {@{work for Wolfram Alpha}@}, although {@{the options for the convention}@} \(see {@{[Fourier transform § Other conventions](#other%20conventions)}@}\) must be {@{changed away from the default option}@}, which is actually equivalent to {@{`integrate cos(6*pi*t) exp(−pi*t^2) exp(i*omega*t) /sqrt(2*pi) from -inf to inf`}@}. <a id="^ref-8"></a>^ref-8 <!--SR:!2025-12-02,20,361!2025-12-01,19,338!2025-12-02,20,363!2025-11-30,18,350!2025-11-30,18,359!2025-12-02,20,361-->

9. In [Gelfand & Shilov 1964](#CITEREFGelfandShilov1964), p. 363, with {@{the non-unitary conventions of this table}@}, {@{the transform of $|\mathbf {x} |^{\lambda }$}@} is given to be {@{$$2^{\lambda +n}\pi ^{ {\tfrac {1}{2} }n}{\frac {\Gamma \left({\frac {\lambda +n}{2} }\right)}{\Gamma \left(-{\frac {\lambda }{2} }\right)} }|{\boldsymbol {\omega } }|^{-\lambda -n}$$}@} from which {@{this follows, with $\lambda =-\alpha$}@}. <a id="^ref-9"></a>^ref-9 <!--SR:!2025-11-29,17,338!2025-12-02,20,359!2025-11-30,18,355!2025-11-30,18,355-->
